        "kids": "Imagine you see a big colorful cloud in space that looks like a shiny bubble made by a star, kind of like blowing soap bubbles. This cloud is called NGC 6072, and it is very special because it has lots of twists and shapes that make it look like a space puzzle. A super cool space camera called the Webb Telescope took a close-up picture using special light we cannot see with our eyes, and it showed red areas where there is nice, cool space gas. Scientists think this amazing cloud got its funny, twisty shape because the star in the middle, which might have some star friends nearby, made bursts of gas that pushed and pulled the cloud into a neat, jumbled mess. It’s like when bubbles pop and make new shapes when you blow them really fast!",
        "original": "Why is this nebula so complex? The Webb Space Telescope has imaged a nebula in great detail that is thought to have emerged from a Sun-like star. NGC 6072 has been resolved into one of the more unusual and complex examples of planetary nebula. The featured image is in infrared light with the red color highlighting cool hydrogen gas. Study of previous images of NGC 6072 indicated several likely outflows and two disks inside the jumbled gas, while the new Webb image resolves new features likely including one disk's edge protruding on the central left. A leading origin hypothesis holds that the nebula's complexity is caused or enhanced by multiple outbursts from a star in a multi-star system near the center.",
        "summarized": "The Webb Space Telescope captured a detailed infrared image of the complex planetary nebula NGC 6072, which likely formed from a Sun-like star. The red color in the image highlights cool hydrogen gas within the nebula. Previous studies suggested several outflows and two disks inside the gas, while the new image reveals additional features including the edge of one disk. The nebula's complexity is thought to result from multiple outbursts from a star in a multi-star system at the center."
